Audit\\n\\n## Summary\\nAudit of the Content Security Policy (CSP) enforcement infrastructure in Firefox located in `dom/security/` directory. The CSP implementation consists of the parser, context/policy enforcement engine, utility functions, and XPCOM interface.\\n\\n## File Inventory\\n\\n### 1. CSP Parser - `dom/security/nsCSPParser.h` and `dom/security/nsCSPParser.cpp`\\n**Primary Class:** `nsCSPParser`\\n**Responsibility:** Parses CSP directive strings into policy objects\\n**Key Methods:**\\n- `parseContentSecurityPolicy()` (static): Main entry point that tokenizes and parses CSP policy strings into `nsCSPPolicy` objects\\n- `policy()`: Begins recursive parsing of the CSP\\n- `directive()`: Parses individual directives\\n- `directiveValue()`: Processes directive source lists\\n- `sourceExpression()`: Parses individual sources (schemes, hosts, keywords, nonces, hashes)\\n\\nThe parser implements a finite state machine pattern following the W3C CSP specification grammar, handling token sequences and validating sources like `'unsafe-inline'`, nonces, hashes, and host expressions.\\n\\n### 2. CSP Context/Policy Enforcer - `dom/security/nsCSPContext.h` and `dom/security/nsCSPContext.cpp`\\n**Primary Class:** `nsCSPContext` (implements `nsIContentSecurityPolicy` interface)\\n**Responsibility:** Main CSP context that holds parsed policies and enforces them at runtime\\n**Key Methods:**\\n- `ShouldLoad()` (line 144 in .cpp): XPCOM interface method that evaluates whether a load is permitted by CSP\\n- `permitsInternal()`: Core evaluation logic for checking if a resource load violates CSP\\n- `ReportInlineViolation()` (line 563 in .cpp): Helper method to report inline script/style violations\\n- `GatherSecurityPolicyViolationEventData()`: Constructs violation event data\\n- `SendReports()`: Dispatches CSP violation reports\\n- `allowsAllInlineBehavior()`: Checks if a directive allows all inline behavior (e.g., 'unsafe-inline')\\n\\nThe context manages multiple CSP policies, handles violation reporting to report-uri endpoints, fires SecurityPolicyViolationEvent events, and provides console logging for violations.\\n\\n### 3. CSP Utilities & Directives - `dom/security/nsCSPUtils.h` and `dom/security/nsCSPUtils.cpp`\\n**Primary Classes:**\\n- `nsCSPDirective`: Base class for all CSP directives\\n- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective`: Specialized class for script-src directive that can restrict script elements, event handlers, and workers\\n- `nsCSPStyleSrcDirective`: For style-src directives\\n- `nsCSPChildSrcDirective`: For child-src directive (backwards compatibility)\\n- Source classes: `nsCSPHostSrc`, `nsCSPSchemeSrc`, `nsCSPKeywordSrc`, `nsCSPNonceSrc`, `nsCSPHashSrc`\\n\\n**Responsibilities:**\\n- Define CSP source matching logic (permits(), allows() methods)\\n- Implement directive-specific behavior (e.g., script-src handling multiple fallback rules)\\n- Handle CSP-related logging and localized error messages\\n- Provide violation data structures\\n\\n**Script-src Evaluation Functions:**\\n- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective::permits()`: Evaluates if a script source is allowed\\n- `nsCSPDirective::allows()`: Checks if a directive allows specific keywords, nonces, or hashes\\n- `allowsAllInlineBehavior()`: Determines if inline scripts are permitted (checks for 'unsafe-inline', nonces, hashes, or strict-dynamic)\\n\\n### 4. XPCOM Interface Declaration - `dom/interfaces/security/nsIContentSecurityPolicy.idl`\\n**Primary Interface:** `nsIContentSecurityPolicy`\\n**Responsibility:** Defines the XPCOM interface for CSP components\\n**Key Methods:**\\n- `ShouldLoad()`: Policy check method called at content load time\\n- Multiple directive enums (CSPDirective): SCRIPT_SRC_DIRECTIVE, SCRIPT_SRC_ELEM_DIRECTIVE, SCRIPT_SRC_ATTR_DIRECTIVE, etc.\\n\\n## Script-src Evaluation for Inline Scripts\\n\\nInline script evaluation occurs primarily in `dom/security/nsCSPContext.cpp` through the following flow:\\n\\n1. **Entry Point:** `ShouldLoad()` method (line 144) receives load requests\\n2. **Policy Matching:** `permitsInternal()` matches the content type to appropriate CSP directives (script-src, script-src-elem, etc.)\\n3. **Inline Script Check:** For inline scripts, the evaluation checks:\\n   - Whether 'unsafe-inline' keyword is present\\n   - Whether the script has a valid nonce matching the policy\\n   - Whether the script hash matches a policy-allowed hash\\n   - Whether 'strict-dynamic' is present (affecting external vs inline)\\n4. **Violation Reporting:** If blocked, `ReportInlineViolation()` is called to:\\n   - Create violation event data via `GatherSecurityPolicyViolationEventData()`\\n   - Fire SecurityPolicyViolationEvent to the page\\n   - Send reports to configured report-uri/report-to endpoints\\n\\nThe `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` class (in nsCSPUtils.h/cpp) holds the actual script-src policy sources and implements the evaluation logic for determining whether inline scripts are allowed based on keywords, nonces, and hashes.\\n\\n## Integration Architecture\\n\\nThe CSP enforcement pipeline:\\n1. **Parsing Stage:** CSP header/meta tags → `nsCSPParser::parseContentSecurityPolicy()` → `nsCSPPolicy` object\\n2. **Storage Stage:** Policy stored in `nsCSPContext` instance associated with Document\\n3. **Enforcement Stage:** When content loads, `nsCSPService` calls `nsCSPContext::ShouldLoad()`\\n4. **Evaluation Stage:** `nsCSPContext` queries appropriate directive (e.g., `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective`) to determine permissibility\\n5. **Reporting Stage:** If violation, `ReportInlineViolation()` dispatches events and HTTP reports\\n\\n## File Relationships\\n\\n- `nsCSPParser` is instantiated by and calls back to `nsCSPContext` during parsing\\n- `nsCSPContext` holds instances of `nsCSPPolicy` which contain `nsCSPDirective` objects\\n- `nsCSPScriptSrcDirective` and other directive classes inherit from `nsCSPDirective` and hold `nsCSPBaseSrc` objects representing individual sources\\n- All three main implementation files (`nsCSPParser.cpp`, `nsCSPContext.cpp`, `nsCSPUtils.cpp`) are compiled together as part of the dom/security module\\n- The XPCOM interface in `.idl` file is the C++ definition language used to generate
